## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The rate typically depends on powers of concentration, but may also involve saturation, autocatalytic, or oscillatory mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- General n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (fractional or integer order rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction or equilibrium offset)
- Mixed order / two-term rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten / saturation kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction)
- Autocatalytic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction with adsorption)
- Power-law with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (general power law with background rate)
- Time-dependent decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or effective third-order process)
- Parallel pathway with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A / (c2 + A) (combined linear and saturating pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power of concentration → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power (A**n for n-th order)
- Concentration in numerator and denominator (rational form in A) → enzyme or surface catalysis with substrate binding/saturation
- Product of concentration and (constant minus concentration), A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth mechanism
- Negative sign in rate law (c0 < 0) → consumption/depletion of reactant A
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Squared denominator (c + A)**2 → competitive adsorption or dual-site surface mechanism
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration → time-varying external conditions (temperature ramp, light intensity)
- Fractional power of concentration A**c1 where 0 < c1 < 1 → diffusion-limited or heterogeneous reaction kinetics
- Constant term independent of A in rate expression → zeroth-order contribution from saturated catalyst or constant external source
- Ratio of polynomials in A with higher degree in denominator → self-inhibition or substrate inhibition at high concentrations
